<div class="mw-parser-output"><p><b>SSBMRank</b> is an annual ranking of the top 100 Super Smash Bros. Melee players previously conducted by <a href="/smash/Melee_It_On_Me" title="Melee It On Me">Melee It On Me</a>, and now conducted by the PG stats team. In order to compile the ranking, top level players, tournament organizers, commentators, and figureheads are asked to rate players on a scale from 1 to 10. The highest and lowest scores for each player is removed, then the scores are averaged to arrive at a final score. For the 2013 ranking, players had to attend at least one US tournament to be eligible, while for the 2014 ranking, they had to place well at a US national (<a href="/smash/Apex_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Apex 2014">Apex 2014</a>, <a href="/smash/2014_MLG_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 MLG Anaheim">2014 MLG Anaheim</a>, <a href="/smash/CEO_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO 2014">CEO 2014</a>, <a href="/smash/EVO_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="EVO 2014">EVO 2014</a>, <a href="/smash/The_Big_House_4" class="mw-redirect" title="The Big House 4">The Big House 4</a>) or attend several US regionals. This criteria excludes skilled players who were not active during the year and international players who did not attend US tournaments. Furthermore, some tournaments at the end of the year were excluded from consideration.
</p><p>The movements up or down in the rankings are relative to the previous years ranking, and not the summer rankings. For example: <a href="/smash/Moky" title="Moky">moky</a> was ranked 96th in 2017 and 46th in the summer of 2018, and ended up with a rank of 52 for the 2018 rankings. The list will not have him move down six spots on the rankings, so instead the list will have him move forty-four spots up.
</p>
